INTRODUCTION

рджреЗрд╡реА рд╕рд░реЛрдЬрд╛рд╕рдирд╕рдореНрднрд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд╛рдордкреНрд░рджрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрд░рд╕реМрд░рднреЗрдпреАред

Mt. ├Вbu L├╗с╣Зiga Vasati Pra┼Ыasti 39.

The present work has been included in the “Gaekwad’s Oriental Series” mainly as a production of a royal prince of m├жdieval Gujar├вt. It is true that the State of Chandr├вvat├о was regarded even at that time as a State of Marwar1,yet the rulers of Chaudr├вvat├о were feudatories (рдорд╣рд╛рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░) of the kings of Gujarat, and even led the Gurjar armies in battlefields. It may be, moreover, noted that the author of the present work has greater claims to be called a Prince of Gujarat in as much as he founded the city of Palanpur.

The dramatic literature of Gujarat. The whole of San╠аskс╣Ыita dramatic literature of India consists of about 600 works. Gujarat’s contribution in this is, however, very small. The following list of San╠аskс╣Ыita dramas of Gujarat hitherto-known will not be without interest.

┬╢ About R├вmachandra’s рдкреНрд░рдмрдиреНрдзрд╢рддthe following note is found in an old paper leaf containing notes on mss. рд░рд╛рдордЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдХреГрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдмрдиреНрдзрд╢рддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реВрдкрдХрдирд╛рдЯрдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдХрдВ релрежрежреж. Hamm├оramadamardana Act I.

Dh├вr├вvarsha and Prahl├вdana. Dh├вr├вvarsha, son of Ya┼Ыodhavala and ruler of Chandr├вvat├о was the elder brother of our author who was his Yuvar├вja. Dh├вr├вvarsha’s reign was very illustrious in the history of the Parmars of Mt. ├Вbu. He fought with the army of Kum├вrap├вla in the invasion of Mallik├вrjuna of Konkana. The present work describes him as having amazed the whole of India with his valour and extolling his skill in archery2, refers to his repelling the nocturnal attack of the King of J├вngalas.^(4)The ms.C identifies this prince with Pс╣Ыithv├оr├вja. The ┼Ъambhar King Pс╣Ыithv├оr├вja was reigning up to Samvat 1236. This most probably may have taken place at the time of the invasion of King Ajayap├вla of the J├вс╣Еgala King.^(5)Dh├вr├вvarsha’s reign was very long. The oldest inscription of his reign yet discovered is dated Samvat 1220. He was living at the time of the laying of the foundation of the L├╗с╣Зigavasti on Mt. ├Вbu, and this event occurred in Samvat 1286. He also helped Vastup├вla3 in repulsing an attack of an army from Delhi about the same time. Prahl├вdana was not fortunate enough to become a king, as he did not outlive his elder brother. From the inscriptions given in Appendix II, it is clear that he was already working as Yuvar├вja in Samvat 1220 and was living up to Samvat 1265.

The form of the play. The P├вrthapar├вkrama is a Vy├вyoga (Military Spectacle). Its main characteristics are that it consists of a single act, the plot is well known and the sentiments are the excited ones. It represents a combat not occasioned by a woman. There are very few female characters

The printed text reads рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рд░реНрддреНрддреЛ incorrectly. The present reading is from a ms. dated Samvat 1507. The meaning of the phrase рд░рдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрддрдпрддрд╛ рдХрдерд╛рдореН is not quite clear. It may mean that Prahl├вdana composed some beautiful prose-romance. But now there is no trace even of its name.

Pra┼Ыasti of the L├╗с╣Зiga Vasati, he represents him as an incarnation of the heavenly cow.┬╣тБ╖

Prahl├вdana the founder of Palanpur. The legend quoted in Appendix III from Upade┼Ыa Tarangiс╣З├оwould show that our author founded after his name the city of Prahl├вdanapura. This city is the same as Palanpur, the capital of the State of that name in Gujarat, 54 miles to the south of Mt. ├Вbu. The State is at present ruled by a Mahomedan Chief who pays to H. H. the Maharaja Gaekwar a tribute of about Rs. 38,000. Here he built a big Jaina temple called P├вlhavih├вra. References to the grandeur of the city and the Vih├вra are found in works of the 13th to 17th centuries.^(18)The legend relates that this prince became a leper through the sin of melting a Jaina metal image and making a bull of it for the Achale┼Ыvara Temple. In order to avert this sin and be cured of leprosy, he resorted to ┼Ъ├оladhavala ├Вch├вrya and at his advice built the P├вlhavih├вra.
